Unexpected (TV series)">Tales of the Unexpected</a></i>, originally aired on <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> between 1979 and 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The series was released to tie in with Dahl\'s <a href="/wiki/Tales_of_the_Unexpected_(book)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tales of the Unexpected (book)">short story anthology of the same name</a>, which had introduced readers to many motifs that were common in his writing.<sup id="cite_ref-totu_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-totu-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The series was an anthology of different tales, initially based on Dahl\'s short stories.<sup id="cite_ref-totu_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-totu-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The stories were sometimes sinister, sometimes wryly comedic and usually had a twist ending. Dahl introduced on camera all the episodes of the first two series, which bore the full title <i>Roald Dahl\'s Tales of the Unexpected</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_and_legacy">Death and legacy</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RoaldDahlgrave.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/RoaldDahlgrave.jpg/220px-RoaldDahlgrave.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/RoaldDahlgrave.jpg/330px-RoaldDahlgrave.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/RoaldDahlgrave.jpg/440px-RoaldDahlgrave.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2108" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RoaldDahlgrave.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dahl\'s gravestone, St Peter and St Paul\'s Church, <a href="/wiki/Great_Missenden" title="Great Missenden">Great Missenden</a>, Buckinghamshire</div></div></div>\n<p>Roald Dahl died on 23 November 1990, at the age of 74 of a rare cancer of the blood, <a href="/wiki/Myelodysplastic_syndrome" title="Myelodysplastic syndrome">myelodysplastic syndrome</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> and was buried in the cemetery at St Peter and St Paul\'s Church in <a href="/wiki/Great_Missenden" title="Great Missenden">Great Missenden</a>, Buckinghamshire, England. According to his granddaughter, the family gave him a "sort of <a href="/wiki/Viking_funeral" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking funeral">Viking funeral</a>". He was buried with his <a href="/wiki/Snooker_cue" class="mw-redirect" title="Snooker cue">snooker cues</a>, some very good <a href="/wiki/Burgundy_wine" title="Burgundy wine">burgundy</a>, chocolates, <a href="/wiki/No._2_pencil" class="mw-redirect" title="No. 2 pencil">HB pencils</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Circular_saw" title="Circular saw">power saw</a>. Today, children continue to leave toys and flowers by his grave.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>  In November 1996, the <a href="/wiki/Roald_Dahl_Children%27s_Gallery" title="Roald Dahl Children&#39;s Gallery">Roald Dahl Children\'s Gallery</a> was opened at the <a href="/wiki/Buckinghamshire_County_Museum" title="Buckinghamshire County Museum">Buckinghamshire County Museum</a> in nearby <a href="/wiki/Aylesbury" title="Aylesbury">Aylesbury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The main-belt asteroid <a href="/wiki/6223_Dahl" title="6223 Dahl">6223 Dahl</a>, discovered by Czech astronomer <a href="/wiki/Anton%C3%ADn_Mrkos" title="Anton\xc3\xadn Mrkos">Anton\xc3\xadn Mrkos</a>, was named in his memory in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-springer-Dahl_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-springer-Dahl-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MPC-Circulars-Archive_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MPC-Circulars-Archive-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;max-width:184px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:"><center>Roald Dahl Plass</center></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Illuminated_Roald_Dahl_Plas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Illuminated_Roald_Dahl_Plas.jpg/180px-Illuminated_Roald_Dahl_Plas.jpg" width="180" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Illuminated_Roald_Dahl_Plas.jpg/270px-Illuminated_Roald_Dahl_Plas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Illuminated_Roald_Dahl_Plas.jpg/360px-Illuminated_Roald_Dahl_Plas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><center>Roald Dahl Plass illuminated at night</center></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Roald_Dahl_Plass_plaque.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Roald_Dahl_Plass_plaque.jpg/180px-Roald_Dahl_Plass_plaque.jpg" width="180" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Roald_Dahl_Plass_plaque.jpg/270px-Roald_Dahl_Plass_plaque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Roald_Dahl_Plass_plaque.jpg/360px-Roald_Dahl_Plass_plaque.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><center>Plaque commemorating Roald Dahl</center></div></div></div></div>\n<p>In 2002, one of <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Bay" title="Cardiff Bay">Cardiff Bay</a>\'s modern landmarks, the Oval Basin plaza, was renamed <i><a href="/wiki/Roald_Dahl_Plass" title="Roald Dahl Plass">Roald Dahl Plass</a></i>. <i>Plass</i> is  Norwegian for "place" or "square", alluding to the writer\'s Norwegian roots. There have also been calls from the public for a permanent statue of him to be erected in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the city celebrated the centenary of Dahl\'s birth in <a href="/wiki/Llandaff" title="Llandaff">Llandaff</a>. Welsh Arts organisations, including <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_Wales" title="National Theatre Wales">National Theatre Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales_Millennium_Centre" title="Wales Millennium Centre">Wales Millennium Centre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Literature_Wales" title="Literature Wales">Literature Wales</a>, came together for a series of events, titled Roald Dahl 100, including a Cardiff-wide City of the Unexpected, which marked his legacy.<sup id="cite_ref-Global_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dahl\'s charitable commitments in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Neurology" title="Neurology">neurology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haematology" class="mw-redirect" title="Haematology">haematology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> during his life have been continued by his widow since his death, through Roald Dahl\'s Marvellous Children\'s Charity, formerly known as the Roald Dahl Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-TELG_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TELG-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The charity provides care and support to seriously ill children and young people throughout the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> In June 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Roald_Dahl_Museum_and_Story_Centre" title="Roald Dahl Museum and Story Centre">Roald Dahl Museum and Story Centre</a> in the author\'s home village <a href="/wiki/Great_Missenden" title="Great Missenden">Great Missenden</a> was officially opened by <a href="/wiki/Cherie_Blair" title="Cherie Blair">Cherie Blair</a>, wife of UK Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>, to celebrate the work of Roald Dahl and advance his work in literacy education.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Over 50,000 visitors from abroad, mainly from Australia, Japan, the United States and Germany, travel to the village museum every year.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Matilda,_Cambridge_Theatre.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Matilda%2C_Cambridge_Theatre.JPG/220px-Matilda%2C_Cambridge_Theatre.JPG" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Matilda%2C_Cambridge_Theatre.JPG/330px-Matilda%2C_Cambridge_Theatre.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Matilda%2C_Cambridge_Theatre.JPG/440px-Matilda%2C_Cambridge_Theatre.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2578" data-file-height="2766" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Matilda,_Cambridge_Theatre.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Matilda_the_Musical" title="Matilda the Musical">Matilda the Musical</a></i> has been shown in the <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">West End</a> since November 2011, and on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a> since April 2013</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2008, the UK charity <a href="/wiki/Booktrust" class="mw-redirect" title="Booktrust">Booktrust</a> and <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Laureate" title="Children&#39;s Laureate">Children\'s Laureate</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Rosen" title="Michael Rosen">Michael Rosen</a> inaugurated The Roald Dahl Funny Prize, an annual award to authors of humorous children\'s fiction.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> On 14 September 2009 (the day after what would have been Dahl\'s 93rd birthday) the first <a href="/wiki/Blue_plaque" title="Blue plaque">blue plaque</a> in his honour was unveiled in Llandaff.<sup id="cite_ref-CDF_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDF-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Rather than commemorating his place of birth, however, the plaque was erected on the wall of the former sweet shop (and site of "The Great Mouse Plot of 1924") that features in the first part of his autobiography <i><a href="/wiki/Boy_(book)" title="Boy (book)">Boy</a></i>. It was unveiled by his widow Felicity and son Theo.<sup id="cite_ref-CDF_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDF-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The anniversary of Dahl\'s birthday on 13 September is celebrated as "Roald Dahl Day" in Africa, the United Kingdom and Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-guard_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In honour of Dahl, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Post_Office" title="Royal Gibraltar Post Office">Royal Gibraltar Post Office</a> issued a set of four stamps in 2010 featuring <a href="/wiki/Quentin_Blake" title="Quentin Blake">Quentin Blake</a>\'s original illustrations for four of the children\'s books written by Dahl during his long career; <i><a href="/wiki/The_BFG" title="The BFG">The BFG</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Twits" title="The Twits">The Twits</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory" title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Matilda_(novel)" title="Matilda (novel)">Matilda</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> A set of six stamps was issued by <a href="/wiki/Royal_Mail" title="Royal Mail">Royal Mail</a> in 2012, featuring Blake\'s illustrations for <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, <i>The Twits</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Witches_(novel)" title="The Witches (novel)">The Witches</a></i>, <i>Matilda</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Mr_Fox" title="Fantastic Mr Fox">Fantastic Mr Fox</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/James_and_the_Giant_Peach" title="James and the Giant Peach">James and the Giant Peach</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_royal_mail_stamps_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_royal_mail_stamps-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Dahl\'s influence has extended beyond literary figures. For instance film director <a href="/wiki/Tim_Burton" title="Tim Burton">Tim Burton</a> recalled from childhood "the second layer [after <a href="/wiki/Dr._Seuss" title="Dr. Seuss">Dr. Seuss</a>] of connecting to a writer who gets the idea of the modern fable \xe2\x80\x93 and the mixture of light and darkness, and not speaking down to kids, and the kind of politically incorrect humour that kids get. I\'ve always like that, and it\'s shaped everything I\'ve felt that I\'ve done."<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> read <i>The BFG</i> to his children when they were young, stating the book celebrates the fact that it\'s OK to be different as well as to have an active imagination: "It\'s very important that we preserve the tradition of allowing young children to run free with their imaginations and magic and imagination are the same thing."<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Actress <a href="/wiki/Scarlett_Johansson" title="Scarlett Johansson">Scarlett Johansson</a> named <i>Fantastic Mr Fox</i> one of the five books that made a difference to her.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:28%;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"Arguably the Shakespeare of children\'s literature, from <i>Fantastic Mr Fox</i> to <i>Matilda</i> and <i>The BFG</i>, filmmakers and animators are still drawing from the enormous vat of material he created."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94"Britain\'s top ten children\'s literature superstars". <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i>, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>Regarded as "one of the greatest storytellers for children of the 20th century",<sup id="cite_ref-IND_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IND-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Dahl was named by <i>The Times</i> one of the 50 greatest British writers since 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-TIM_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TIM-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He ranks amongst the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_fiction_authors" title="List of best-selling fiction authors">world\'s best-selling fiction authors</a> with sales estimated at over 250&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_2016_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2016-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BDC_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BDC-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-INT_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INT-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and his books have been published in almost 60 languages.<sup id="cite_ref-Global_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In 2003 four books by Dahl, led by <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i> at number 35, ranked among the Top 100 in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Big_Read" title="The Big Read">The Big Read</a></i>, a survey of the British public by the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> to determine the "nation\'s best-loved novel" of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> In surveys of UK teachers, parents and students, Dahl is frequently ranked the best children\'s writer.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In a 2006 list for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_of_Literature" title="Royal Society of Literature">Royal Society of Literature</a>, Harry Potter creator <a href="/wiki/J._K._Rowling" title="J. K. Rowling">J. K. Rowling</a> named <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i> one of her top ten books every child should read.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, <i>Matilda</i> was ranked number 30 among all-time best children\'s novels in a survey published by <i><a href="/wiki/School_Library_Journal" title="School Library Journal">School Library Journal</a></i>, a monthly with primarily U.S. audience. The Top 100 included four books by Dahl, more than any other writer: <i>Matilda</i>, <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, <i>The Witches</i>, and <i>The BFG</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-SLJChapter2012_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SLJChapter2012-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, Dahl was among the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">British cultural icons</a> selected by artist Sir <a href="/wiki/Peter_Blake_(artist)" title="Peter Blake (artist)">Peter Blake</a> to appear in a new version of his most famous artwork \xe2\x80\x93 the Beatles\' <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper&#39;s Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper\'s Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i> album cover \xe2\x80\x93 to celebrate the British cultural figures of his life he most admires.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In a 2017 UK poll of the greatest authors, songwriters, artists and photographers, Dahl was named the greatest storyteller of all time, ranking ahead of <a href="/wiki/Dickens" class="mw-redirect" title="Dickens">Dickens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a>, Rowling and Spielberg.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, the airline <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian Air">Norwegian</a> announced Dahl\xe2\x80\x99s image would appear on the tail fin one of their <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800</a> aircraft. He is one of the company\'s six "British tail fin heroes", joining Queen frontman <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a>, England World Cup winner <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Moore" title="Bobby Moore">Bobby Moore</a>, novelist <a href="/wiki/Jane_Austen" title="Jane Austen">Jane Austen</a>, pioneering pilot <a href="/wiki/Amy_Johnson" title="Amy Johnson">Amy Johnson</a> and aviation entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Laker" title="Freddie Laker">Freddie Laker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Publications">Publications</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Roald_Dahl_bibliography" title="Roald Dahl bibliography">Roald Dahl bibliography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roald_Dahl_short_stories_bibliography" title="Roald Dahl short stories bibliography">Roald Dahl short stories bibliography</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 25em; -webkit-column-width: 25em; column-width: 25em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.loc.gov/nls/about/organization/standards-guidelines/qrst/#r">"NLS: Say How, A-D"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.
